# Ingestion Status Summary

## Standing Scope

Use these source classes autonomously:

- local corpus at `/Users/saumyamehta/DS interview prep/books`;
- `system_design_vault/` notes;
- official product docs;
- official/open white papers;
- official university course pages, lecture notes, and official YouTube playlists or recordings;
- official engineering blogs and provider examples when they carry primary implementation guidance.

Do not use:

- Anna's Archive, LibGen, Z-Library, or shadow-library downloads;
- raw book text dumps;
- long excerpts;
- TOC-only or source-outline "first pass" notes;
- third-party lecture transcript sites as source truth.

## Current File Hygiene

## Control-Plane Notes

- `05-ingestion-runs/unresolved-high-value-book-gaps.md` is the trigger-based queue for the remaining local book slices that are still worth deepening when a concrete route or release-gate gap appears.
- `05-ingestion-runs/urgent-blockers.json` is the machine-readable overnight blocker file. The nightly orchestrator should keep it current, and the blocker-ping cron job should only notify when a real user-facing blocker exists.


- Local corpus scope is limited to allowed file types: PDF and DOCX are currently present; JPEG/JPG/DOC remain allowed if added later.
- Current local corpus count: 34 allowed files. The macOS `.DS_Store` folder metadata file is ignored and not treated as corpus material.
- Duplicate to avoid double-ingestion: `AI Engineering.pdf` and `Chip Huyen - AI Engineering_ Building Applications with Foundation Models (2025, O'Reilly Media).pdf`.

## Found

- Core local books for Agent Studio: AI Engineering, Inference Engineering, LLM Engineers Handbook, Designing Machine Learning Systems, Practical MLOps, Building ML Powered Applications, Build a Large Language Model From Scratch, Prompt Engineering for LLMs.
- Official/open local foundations: ISLP, Bishop PRML, Deep Learning, Machine Learning: A Probabilistic Perspective, and Speech and Language Processing.
- Official Stanford lecture sources: CS329S, CS224N, CS25, CS324, CS336, CS231n.
- Official docs/white papers: OpenAI evals and agent evals, Anthropic prompting, Google Cloud RAG and GenAI ops, AWS Well-Architected GenAI Lens, AWS GenAI security, pgvector, LangChain/LangGraph, OpenAI Realtime/Agents, Google ADK/A2A.

Covers: 12a six-stage pipeline inside `run_grpo_train_step()`, 12b variant dispatch matrix (GRPO/Dr.GRPO/RFT/MaxRL + noclip/grpo/gspo off-policy), 12c implicit microbatch decomposition, 12d three system-design implications (text↔tensor boundary, frame-shifted parallelism, missing per-microbatch observability).

- Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-silent-default-gaps-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready Stanford maintenance note grounded in the official TRL GRPO docs plus the CS336 Assignment 5 public surface. The note cross-references TRL `GRPOConfig` defaults (`beta=0.0`, `loss_type=None`, `num_iterations=1`, `scale_rewards=True`, `use_vllm=False`, `vllm_importance_sampling_correction=True`) against the A5 reward surface to identify silent-default paths where a library default can silently kill the reward signal or change the effective objective without the operator being warned. Covers 8 gap categories: disabled KL drift anchor, length-biased loss normalization, inactive clipping surrogate, group-std difficulty weighting, in-process vs vLLM generation mismatch, silent TIS objective modification, `max_new_tokens` inherited-default trap, and dual-path stop-string handling.

- Four vault-gap cross-check notes added under `01-sources/official-open/` on 2026-05-19, deepening anchor notes with primary-source artifacts for gap areas identified in the research-artifacts task:
  1. `deep-learning-optimization-stability-cross-check.md` -- LayerNorm (arXiv:1607.06450), RMSNorm (arXiv:1910.07467), Pascanu et al. gradient clipping (arXiv:1211.5063), Mamba/SSM (arXiv:2312.00752), and GroupNorm (arXiv:1803.08494) cross-checked against the Deep Learning anchor note's numerical-stability, gradient-management, and sequence-model design rules. Adds normalization-strategy, gradient-clipping-policy, and sequence-model-family fields.
  2. `gan-evaluation-training-cross-check.md` -- StyleGAN3/Alias-Free GAN (arXiv:2106.12423), FID/TTUR (arXiv:1706.08500), KID (arXiv:1801.01473), and spectral normalization (arXiv:1802.05957) cross-checked against the GANs in Action anchor note's evaluation, stability, and latent-control design rules. Adds stability-method, distribution-metric-assumptions, equivariance-check, and TTUR compliance fields.
  3. `nlp-adapter-recipes-cross-check.md` -- spaCy 3.x pipeline architecture, HuggingFace tokenizers four-stage pipeline (normalizer, pre-tokenizer, model, post-processor), and modern NER approaches cross-checked against the Python NLP Cookbook anchor note's adapter contracts, normalization policies, and extraction design rules. Decomposes normalization into four stages, adds NER approach type, and tokenizer-embedding alignment gate.
  4. `bayesian-uncertainty-deepening-cross-check.md` -- Conformal prediction (arXiv:2107.07511), Bayesian deep learning generalization (arXiv:2002.03704), MC Dropout (arXiv:1506.02142), and temperature scaling (arXiv:1706.02599) cross-checked against the Probabilistic ML Advanced anchor note's uncertainty-bearing route design rules. Adds conformal_prediction_record, calibration method, uncertainty framework declaration, and exchangeability/shift coverage fields.
  The MOC, deep-reading coverage ledger, status summary, and source-record manifests are updated to include the four new cross-check notes.

## HF TrainingArguments silent-defaults pipeline cross-check — 2026-05-24 (extended pass)

|- Added `01-sources/official-open/hf-training-args-silent-defaults-pipeline-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready companion to the TRL GRPO silent-defaults note. Traces the three-layer inheritance chain (`TrainingArguments` → `_BaseConfig` → `GRPOConfig`) using TRL v1.4.0 and Transformers v5.9.0 installed source code to identify 10 critical silent-default categories where the middle `_BaseConfig` layer silently flips `bf16`, `gradient_checkpointing`, and `logging_steps`. Identifies `generation_config` non-preservation in checkpoint resume as the highest-risk RL gotcha (resuming with greedy decoding after crash). Covers: `_BaseConfig` auto-bf16, `remove_unused_columns`|`learning_rate` overrides, `generation_kwargs` hardcoded in `grpo_trainer.py` line 802, `use_ref_model` conditional on `beta != 0.0`, `eval_strategy=no` silent metric gap, `top_k=50` silent action-space cap, `save_total_limit=None` unbounded disk growth, `max_tool_calling_iterations=None→sys.maxsize` agentic loop risk, and 6-item checkpoint-resume gap list.

- Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-code-anatomy-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready code-level grounding of the TRL GRPOTrainer training loop. Covers: 8 loss variant dispatch architecture (default loss_type="dapo" — not the original GRPO from the DeepSeekMath paper), per-token KL formula with beta=0.0 disabling the reference model entirely, group-based reward normalization with cross-process gather, two-sided clipping on importance sampling ratios, micro-batch buffer reuse with stale-generation risk, and 17 doc-to-code gaps identified during code read. The key finding: TRL's default loss_type="dapo" uses global token normalization (not sequence-level), and default beta=0.0 means the reference model is never loaded — 2× memory savings, but zero KL regularization with no warning emitted.
- Added `01-sources/official-open/assets/trl-grpo-training-loop-code-anatomy.svg` as a mental-model artifact showing the two-phase training loop (generation → training) with loss variant dispatch and silent-default risk zones.

|## Datasets-TRL per-library-default composition cross-check — 2026-05-24
|
||- Added `01-sources/official-open/datasets-trl-silent-defaults-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready per-library-default end-to-end composition cross-check. Traces datasets library default parameters through the TRL GRPOTrainer data pipeline to identify 8 composition-level silent failure modes that individual-library cross-checks do not catch. Key findings: (1) `load_from_cache_file=None→True` + TRL no override = silent stale cache reuse across preprocessing changes; (2) `map(batched=False)` + TRL no override = wrong single-row tokenization with padding/truncation; (3) `map(remove_columns=None)` + TRL `remove_unused_columns=False` = intentional column pass-through but accidental reward-function surface contamination; (4) `train_test_split(seed=None)` + TRL no override = non-reproducible train/eval splits across experiments; (5) `select()` lacking cache_file param = mandatory disk cache on every TRL eval callback call; (6) `shard(contiguous=True)` default = distribution bias risk for distributed settings; (7) `IterableDataset.shuffle(buffer_size=1000)` = approximate shuffling (GRPOTrainer explicitly rejects IterableDataset); (8) `_CACHING_ENABLED = True` global singleton = all cache-eligible operations silently reuse cached results.
||- Generated `01-sources/official-open/assets/datasets-trl-default-composition.svg` showing the 6-layer datasets→TRL default composition chain with HIGH/MEDIUM risk indicators.
||- Linked note and SVG in MOC.md.
||- Rechecked Stanford availability on 2026-05-24. No queue-changing delta: CS336 L16 still visible (2 refs), L17 commented-out, A5 at `495ea2b`, CS25 May 21/28 abstract-only, recordings unchanged.

|## TRL GRPOTrainer reward function composition cross-check — 2026-05-25
|
||- Added `01-sources/official-open/trl-grpo-reward-composition-cross-check.md` as a canon-ready code-level grounding of GRPOTrainer's multi-reward dispatch, reward normalization, and token-level vs sequence-level loss aggregation. Based on deep-read of TRL v1.4.0 source code (grpo_trainer.py lines 393-447, 1196-1285, 2143-2180, 2437-2588) corroborated against the DeepSeekMath GRPO paper (2402.03300), DAPO paper (2503.14476), and GDPO paper (2601.05242).
||- **Key findings**: (1) Two multi-reward aggregation modes — `sum_then_normalize` (default, group-normalizes combined scalar) and `normalize_then_sum` (GDPO-inspired, per-function z-score normalization before sum). (2) Three `scale_rewards` modes — "group" (GRPO paper default), "batch", "none" — all reducing to sequence-level advantage broadcast to all token positions. (3) 8 loss_type variants differ only in loss aggregation normalizer (sequence-length mean → global token count → constant divisor → length-weighted), not in advantage computation. (4) DAPO loss_type in TRL implements token-level normalization correctly but **misses** Dynamic Sampling filter (all-correct/all-incorrect prompts) and Overlong Reward Shaping. (5) No per-token reward computation exists anywhere in GRPOTrainer — all rewards are sequence-level scalars, consistent with the original GRPO paper. (6) GDPO per-function normalization prevents the signal-collapse problem where summing raw multi-rewards before normalization causes identical advantage values.
||- Generated `01-sources/official-open/assets/trl-grpo-reward-composition-pipeline.svg` showing the 4-phase pipeline (reward → combination → advantage → loss) with configuration alternatives for each phase.
||- Linked note and SVG in MOC.md.
||- Rechecked Stanford availability on 2026-05-25. No queue-changing delta: CS336 L16 still visible (lecture_16.pdf, HTTP 200), L17 commented-out HTML (spring2026-lectures repo still 404, expected Wed May 27), A5 at `495ea2b` (unchanged). CS25 recordings page JS-rendered; no new recordings found. Local-book gaps: record_count remains 0.
||- Updated `MOC.md`, `status-summary.md`, `nightly-automation-log.md`, `unresolved-high-value-book-gaps.json`, and `urgent-blockers.json` so future runs discover the new reward composition cross-check while preserving zero unresolved local-book gaps and zero active blockers.

## Accelerate ↔ TRL silent-failure interaction cross-check — 2026-05-26 (03:00 CDT)

- Added `01-sources/official-open/accelerate-trl-silent-failure-interactions.md` as a canon-ready code-level analysis of 7 silent-failure interactions between `accelerate.Accelerator.__init__()` defaults and `trl.GRPOTrainer` (via `transformers.Trainer`). Based on deep-read of accelerate(accelerator.py:279-302, 546-556, 693-750, 2866-2900), TRL GRPOTrainer(lines 494-603, 1031-1035, 2351-2585), and transformers Trainer(lines 693-810, 1700-1772).
- **Key findings**: (1) Trainer overrides 3 defaults(gradient_accumulation_steps forced to 1, mixed_precision passed from TrainingArgs, kwargs_handlers hardcoded to DDP-only) but silently inherits 4(device_placement=True, step_scheduler_with_optimizer=True, split_batches=False, dispatch_batches=None). (2) `step_scheduler_with_optimizer=True`(inherited) + Trainer manual `lr_scheduler.step()` causes double LR stepping — cosine schedules reach zero at 50% training silently. (3) `device_placement=True` pre-moves model to GPU before DeepSpeed/FSDP wrapping, causing OOM. (4) `mixed_precision="no"` from TrainingArguments default runs full fp32 with 2× VRAM and no warning. (5) GA plugin forced to 1 means `accelerator.sync_gradients` fires every micro-batch.
- Generated `accelerate-trl-interaction-cascade.svg` showing 3-layer chain with 6 failure mode cards(1 Critical, 3 High, 2 Medium).
- Linked note and SVG in MOC.md.
- **Stanford recheck(03:00 CDT)**: No queue changes. L16 visible, L17 commented-out, spring2026 repo 404, A5 still `495ea2b`. CS25 no new recordings.
- Updated `MOC.md`, `status-summary.md`, `nightly-automation-log.md`, `unresolved-high-value-book-gaps.json`, and `urgent-blockers.json`. Zero unresolved local-book gaps preserved(record_count=0). Zero active blockers.

## GDL Ch5 autoregressive models promotion — 2026-06-01 02:04 UTC (extended)

- **What changed**: Generative Deep Learning Chapter 5 (autoregressive models) promoted from `deep_read_pass_1` to `canon_ready`. Expanded from 89-line thin note (LSTM gate summary only) to ~180-line canon-ready note covering: LSTM 6-step gate mechanics with cell-state gradient highway, cell state vs hidden state distinction, embedding layer semantics (trainable lookup table, `vocab_size × embedding_size`), tokenization choices (word vs character), temperature sampling as decode policy, stacked LSTMs vs GRU simplification, autoregressive sequential decoding bottleneck for production serving, and system-design implications (temperature as effective data-distribution modulator, stop-policy effects, cell vs hidden state for RL signal collection).
- **Cross-check written**: `01-sources/official-open/gdl-ch5-autoregressive-cross-check.md` corroborates GDL Ch5 against DL Ch10 (long-dependency failure modes, gated recurrence) and AI Engineering Ch9 (production inference optimization). Notes three system-design gaps in GDL's treatment: training vs inference asymmetry (teacher forcing vs autoregressive), no production latency/throughput metrics, and PixelCNN as ML knowledge rather than system-relevant.
